       </a>

        </td>
       </tr>

      <p>
       <b>
        Quebec
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          (
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'w' in 'wind'">
            w
           </span>
          </span>
          )
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-Quebec.ogv" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/En-ca-Quebec.oga" title="En-ca-Quebec.oga">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oedpron_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-oedpron-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French:
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         Québec
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [kebɛk]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:FR-Qu%C3%A9bec.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/FR-Qu%C3%A9bec.ogg" title="FR-Québec.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EFname_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EFname-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is one of the thirteen
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">
        provinces and territories of Canada
       </a>
       . It is bordered to the west by the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">
        Ontario
       </a>
       and the bodies of water
       <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">
        James Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">
        Hudson Bay
       </a>
       ; to the north by
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Strait" title="Hudson Strait">
        Hudson Strait
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Bay" title="Ungava Bay">
        Ungava Bay
       </a>
       ; to the east by the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">
        Gulf of Saint Lawrence
       </a>
       and the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland and Labrador
       </a>
       ; and to the south by the province of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">
        New Brunswick
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. states
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
        Maine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">
        New Hampshire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
        Vermont
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
        New York
       </a>
       . It also shares
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">
        maritime borders
       </a>
       with Nunavut,
       <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">
        Prince Edward Island
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">
        Nova Scotia
       </a>
       . Quebec is Canada's largest province by area and its second-largest administrative division; only the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">
        Nunavut
       </a>
       is larger. It is historically and politically considered to be part of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Canada" title="Central Canada">
        Central Canada
       </a>
       (with Ontario).
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_population" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by population">
        second-most
       </a>
       populous province of
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       , after Ontario.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is the only one to have a predominantly
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_French_is_an_official_language" title="List of territorial entities where French is an official language">
        French-speaking
       </a>
       population, with
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       as the sole provincial
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       . Most inhabitants live in urban areas near the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">
        Saint Lawrence River
       </a>
       between
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
        Quebec City
       </a>
       , the capital. Approximately half of Quebec residents live in the Greater Montreal Area, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Montreal" title="Island of Montreal">
        Island of Montreal
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-speaking_Quebecer" title="English-speaking Quebecer">
        English-speaking communities
       </a>
       and English-language institutions are concentrated in the west of the island of Montreal but are also significantly present in the
       <a href="/wiki/Outaouais" title="Outaouais">
        Outaouais
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Townships" title="Eastern Townships">
        Eastern Townships
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">
        Gaspé
       </a>
       regions. The
       <a href="/wiki/Nord-du-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Nord-du-Québec">
        Nord-du-Québec
       </a>
       region, occupying the northern half of the province, is sparsely populated and inhabited primarily by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_in_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples in Canada">
        Aboriginal peoples
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The climate around the major cities is four-season
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        continental
       </a>
       with cold and snowy winters combined with warm to hot humid summers, but further north long winter seasons dominate and as a result the northern areas of the province are marked by
       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">
        tundra
       </a>
       conditions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even in central Quebec, at comparatively southerly latitudes, winters are severe in inland areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_sovereignty_movement" title="Quebec sovereignty movement">
        Quebec independence
       </a>
       debates have played a large role in the
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Quebec" title="Politics of Quebec">
        politics of the province
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">
        Parti Québécois
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Quebec" title="Government of Quebec">
        governments
       </a>
       held referendums on
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
        sovereignty
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_referendum,_1980" title="Quebec referendum, 1980">
        1980
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_referendum,_1995" title="Quebec referendum, 1995">
        1995
       </a>
       ; both were voted down by voters, the latter defeated by a very narrow margin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-georgetown1_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-georgetown1-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2006, the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_Canada" title="House of Commons of Canada">
        House of Commons of Canada
       </a>
       passed
       <a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois_nation_motion" title="Québécois nation motion">
        a symbolic motion
       </a>
       recognizing the "
       <a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois_people" title="Québécois people">
        Québécois
       </a>
       as a nation within a united Canada."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While the province's substantial
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">
        natural resources
       </a>
       have long been the mainstay of its economy, sectors of the
       <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">
        knowledge economy
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">
        aerospace
       </a>
       , information and communication technologies,
       <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
        biotechnology
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">
        pharmaceutical industry
       </a>
       also play leading roles. These many industries have all contributed to helping Quebec become an economically influential province within Canada, second only to Ontario in economic output.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_boundary_changes">
        Etymology and boundary changes
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="458" data-file-width="640" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg/220px-Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg/330px-Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg/440px-Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samuel_de_Champlain_arrive_%C3%A0_Qu%C3%A9bec_-_George_Agnew_Reid_-_1909.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The arrival of
         <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">
          Samuel de Champlain
         </a>
         , the father of
         <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">
          New France
         </a>
         , on the site of
         <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
          Quebec City
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The name "Québec", which comes from the
       <a href="/wiki/Algonquin_language" title="Algonquin language">
        Algonquin
       </a>
       word
       <i>
        kébec
       </i>
       meaning "where the river narrows", originally referred to the area around Quebec City where the Saint Lawrence River narrows to a cliff-lined gap. Early variations in the spelling of the name included
       <i>
        Québecq
       </i>
       (Levasseur, 1601) and
       <i>
        Kébec
       </i>
       (Lescarbot, 1609).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French explorer
       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">
        Samuel de Champlain
       </a>
       chose the name
       <i>
        Québec
       </i>
       in 1608 for the colonial outpost he would use as the administrative seat for the French colony of
       <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">
        New France
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The province is sometimes referred to as "La belle province" ("The beautiful province").
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763%E2%80%931791)" title="Province of Quebec (1763–1791)">
        Province of Quebec
       </a>
       was founded in the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Proclamation_of_1763" title="Royal Proclamation of 1763">
        Royal Proclamation of 1763
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">
        Treaty of Paris
       </a>
       formally transferred the
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
        French colony
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">
        Canada
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to Britain after the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
        Seven Years' War
       </a>
       . The proclamation restricted the province to an area along the banks of the Saint Lawrence River. The
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">
        Quebec Act
       </a>
       of 1774 expanded the territory of the province to include the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">
        Great Lakes
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">
        Ohio River
       </a>
       Valley and south of
       <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">
        Rupert's Land
       </a>
       , more or less restoring the borders previously existing under French rule before the Conquest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geographers1968_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geographers1968-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">
        Treaty of Versailles
       </a>
       ceded territories south of the Great Lakes to the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PeirceCo1877_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PeirceCo1877-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Act_of_1791" title="Constitutional Act of 1791">
        Constitutional Act of 1791
       </a>
       , the territory was divided between
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">
        Lower Canada
       </a>
       (present-day Quebec) and
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">
        Upper Canada
       </a>
       (present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">
        Ontario
       </a>
       ), with each being granted an elected legislative assembly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KelleyTrebilcock2010_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-KelleyTrebilcock2010-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1840, these become
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_East" title="Canada East">
        Canada East
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">
        Canada West
       </a>
       after the British Parliament unified Upper and Lower Canada into the
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">
        Province of Canada
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnston1881_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Johnston1881-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This territory was redivided into the Provinces of Quebec and Ontario at
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">
        Confederation
       </a>
       in 1867.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LinteauDurocher1983_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LinteauDurocher1983-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each became one of the first four
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">
        provinces
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1870, Canada purchased
       <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">
        Rupert's Land
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson's Bay Company">
        Hudson's Bay Company
       </a>
       and over the next few decades the
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada" title="Parliament of Canada">
        Parliament of Canada
       </a>
       transferred to Quebec portions of this territory that would more than triple the size of the province.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1898, the Canadian Parliament passed the first
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Boundary_Extension_Act,_1898" title="Quebec Boundary Extension Act, 1898">
        Quebec Boundary Extension Act
       </a>
       that expanded the provincial boundaries northward to include the lands of the local
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_in_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples in Canada">
        aboriginal peoples
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morantz2002_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morantz2002-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was followed by the addition of the
       <a href="/wiki/District_of_Ungava" title="District of Ungava">
        District of Ungava
       </a>
       through the
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Boundaries_Extension_Act,_1912" title="Quebec Boundaries Extension Act, 1912">
        Quebec Boundaries Extension Act of 1912
       </a>
       that added the northernmost lands of the
       <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">
        Inuit
       </a>
       to create the modern Province of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morantz2002_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morantz2002-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1927, the border between Quebec and
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland and Labrador
       </a>
       was established by the British
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">
        Judicial Committee of the Privy Council
       </a>
       . Quebec
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labrador_boundary_dispute" title="Labrador boundary dispute">
        officially disputes this boundary
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Quebec" title="Geography of Quebec">
        Geography of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Quebec.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="800" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Quebec.png/220px-Map_of_Quebec.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Quebec.png/330px-Map_of_Quebec.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Quebec.png/440px-Map_of_Quebec.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Quebec.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Quebec
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Canada" title="Eastern Canada">
        eastern part
       </a>
       of Canada, and (from a historical and political perspective) part of Central Canada, Quebec occupies a territory nearly three times the size of France or Texas, most of which is very sparsely populated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its topography is very different from one region to another due to the varying composition of the ground, the climate (latitude and altitude), and the proximity to water. The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        Saint Lawrence Lowland
       </a>
       (south) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">
        Canadian Shield
       </a>
       (north) are the two main topographic regions, and are radically different.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elson_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Elson-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">
        Hydrography
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Quebec has one of the world's largest reserves of
       <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">
        fresh water
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       occupying 12% of its surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabin198639_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabin198639-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has 3% of the world's renewable fresh water, whereas it has only 0.1% of its population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More than half a million lakes,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including 30 with an area greater than 250 square kilometres (97 sq mi), and 4,500 rivers
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025_30-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_of_Quebec20025-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       pour their torrents into the Atlantic Ocean, through the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">
        Gulf of Saint Lawrence
       </a>
       and the Arctic Ocean, by
       <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">
        James
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">
        Hudson
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Bay" title="Ungava Bay">
        Ungava
       </a>
       bays. The largest inland body of water is the
       <a href="/wiki/Caniapiscau_Reservoir" title="Caniapiscau Reservoir">
        Caniapiscau Reservoir
       </a>
       , created in the realization of the
       <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Project" title="James Bay Project">
        James Bay Project
       </a>
       to produce hydroelectric power.
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mistassini" title="Lake Mistassini">
        Lake Mistassini
       </a>
       is the largest natural lake in Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTQ-resC_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CTQ-resC-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg/220px-Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg/330px-Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg/440px-Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chutes_%C3%A0_Michel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Michel's falls on
         <a href="/wiki/Ashuapmushuan_River" title="Ashuapmushuan River">
          Ashuapmushuan River
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-F%C3%A9licien,_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Saint-Félicien, Québec">
          Saint-Félicien
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Saguenay%E2%80%93Lac-Saint-Jean" title="Saguenay–Lac-Saint-Jean">
          Saguenay–Lac-Saint-Jean
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">
        Saint Lawrence River
       </a>
       has some of the world's largest sustaining inland Atlantic ports at Montreal (the province's largest city),
       <a href="/wiki/Trois-Rivi%C3%A8res" title="Trois-Rivières">
        Trois-Rivières
       </a>
       , and Quebec City (the capital). Its access to the Atlantic Ocean and the interior of North America made it the base of early
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">
        French exploration and settlement
       </a>
       in the 17th and 18th centuries. Since 1959, the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Seaway" title="Saint Lawrence Seaway">
        Saint Lawrence Seaway
       </a>
       has provided a navigable link between the Atlantic Ocean and the Great Lakes. Northeast of Quebec City, the river broadens into the world's largest
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuary
       </a>
       , the feeding site of numerous species of whales, fish, and seabirds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The river empties into the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">
        Gulf of Saint Lawrence
       </a>
       . This marine environment sustains fisheries and smaller ports in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bas-Saint-Laurent" title="Bas-Saint-Laurent">
        Lower Saint Lawrence
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Bas-Saint-Laurent
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Côte-Nord">
        Lower North Shore
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Côte-Nord
       </i>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">
        Gaspé
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Gaspésie
       </i>
       ) regions of the province. The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">
        Saint Lawrence River
       </a>
       with its
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">
        estuary
       </a>
       forms the basis of Quebec's development through the centuries. At the same time, many affluent rivers testify to the exploration of land, among them
       <a href="/wiki/Ashuapmushuan_River" title="Ashuapmushuan River">
        Ashuapmushuan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chaudi%C3%A8re_River" title="Chaudière River">
        Chaudière
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gatineau_River" title="Gatineau River">
        Gatineau
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manicouagan_River" title="Manicouagan River">
        Manicouagan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_River" title="Ottawa River">
        Ottawa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Richelieu_River" title="Richelieu River">
        Richelieu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rupert_River" title="Rupert River">
        Rupert
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saguenay_River" title="Saguenay River">
        Saguenay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint-Fran%C3%A7ois_River" title="Saint-François River">
        Saint-François
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saint-Maurice_River" title="Saint-Maurice River">
        Saint-Maurice
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">
        Topography
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scotora2_PJC.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Scotora2_PJC.jpg/220px-Scotora2_PJC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Scotora2_PJC.jpg/330px-Scotora2_PJC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Scotora2_PJC.jpg/440px-Scotora2_PJC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scotora2_PJC.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Cartier_River" title="Jacques-Cartier River">
          Jacques-Cartier River
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec's highest point at 1,652 metres is Mont d'Iberville, known in English as
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Caubvick" title="Mount Caubvick">
        Mount Caubvick
       </a>
       , located on the border with
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland and Labrador
       </a>
       in the northeastern part of the province, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Torngat_Mountains" title="Torngat Mountains">
        Torngat Mountains
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most populous
       <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">
        physiographic
       </a>
       region is the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        Saint Lawrence Lowland
       </a>
       . It extends northeastward from the southwestern portion of the province along the shores of the Saint Lawrence River to the Quebec City region, limited to the North by the
       <a href="/wiki/Laurentian_Mountains" title="Laurentian Mountains">
        Laurentian Mountains
       </a>
       and to the South by the
       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">
        Appalachians
       </a>
       . It mainly covers the areas of the
       <a href="/wiki/Centre-du-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Centre-du-Québec">
        Centre-du-Québec
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laval_(Qu%C3%A9bec)" title="Laval (Québec)">
        Laval
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mont%C3%A9r%C3%A9gie" title="Montérégie">
        Montérégie
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration_of_Montreal" title="Urban agglomeration of Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       , the southern regions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Capitale-Nationale" title="Capitale-Nationale">
        Capitale-Nationale
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lanaudi%C3%A8re" title="Lanaudière">
        Lanaudière
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Laurentides" title="Laurentides">
        Laurentides
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauricie" title="Mauricie">
        Mauricie
       </a>
       and includes
       <a href="/wiki/Anticosti_Island" title="Anticosti Island">
        Anticosti Island
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mingan_Archipelago" title="Mingan Archipelago">
        Mingan Archipelago
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and other small islands of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_St._Lawrence_lowland_forests" title="Gulf of St. Lawrence lowland forests">
        Gulf of St. Lawrence lowland forests
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
        ecoregion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAC_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NAC-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its landscape is low-lying and flat, except for isolated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Igneous" title="Igneous">
        igneous
       </a>
       outcrops near Montreal called the
       <a href="/wiki/Monteregian_Hills" title="Monteregian Hills">
        Monteregian Hills
       </a>
       , formerly covered by the waters of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">
        Lake Champlain
       </a>
       . The Oka hills also rise from the plain. Geologically, the lowlands formed as a
       <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">
        rift valley
       </a>
       about 100 million years ago and are prone to infrequent but significant earthquakes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elson_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Elson-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most recent layers of
       <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">
        sedimentary rock
       </a>
       were formed as the seabed of the ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Champlain_Sea" title="Champlain Sea">
        Champlain Sea
       </a>
       at the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_glaciation" title="Wisconsin glaciation">
        last ice age
       </a>
       about 14,000 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The combination of rich and easily arable soils and Quebec's relatively warm climate makes this valley the most prolific agricultural area of Quebec province.
       <a href="/wiki/Mixed_Wood_Plains_Ecozone_(CEC)" title="Mixed Wood Plains Ecozone (CEC)">
        Mixed forests
       </a>
       provide most of Canada's springtime
       <a href="/wiki/Maple_syrup" title="Maple syrup">
        maple syrup
       </a>
       crop. The rural part of the landscape is divided into narrow rectangular tracts of land that extend from the river and date back to
       <a href="/wiki/Seigneurial_system_of_New_France" title="Seigneurial system of New France">
        settlement patterns in 17th century New France
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="567" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg/220px-Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg/330px-Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg/440px-Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Automne-manche_d%27%C3%A9p%C3%A9e_592K_-2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Autumn landscape of
         <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">
          Haute-Gaspésie
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       More than 95% of Quebec's territory lies within the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">
        Canadian Shield
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is generally a quite flat and exposed mountainous terrain interspersed with higher points such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Laurentian_Mountains" title="Laurentian Mountains">
        Laurentian Mountains
       </a>
       in southern Quebec, the
       <a href="/wiki/Otish_Mountains" title="Otish Mountains">
        Otish Mountains
       </a>
       in central Quebec and the
       <a href="/wiki/Torngat_Mountains" title="Torngat Mountains">
        Torngat Mountains
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Bay" title="Ungava Bay">
        Ungava Bay
       </a>
       . The topography of the Shield has been shaped by glaciers from the successive ice ages, which explains the glacial deposits of boulders, gravel and sand, and by sea water and post-glacial lakes that left behind thick deposits of clay in parts of the Shield. The Canadian Shield also has a complex hydrological network of perhaps a million lakes, bogs, streams and rivers. It is rich in the forestry, mineral and hydro-electric resources that are a mainstay of the Quebec economy.
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">
        Primary industries
       </a>
       sustain small cities in regions of
       <a href="/wiki/Abitibi-T%C3%A9miscamingue" title="Abitibi-Témiscamingue">
        Abitibi-Témiscamingue
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saguenay%E2%80%93Lac-Saint-Jean" title="Saguenay–Lac-Saint-Jean">
        Saguenay–Lac-Saint-Jean
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Côte-Nord">
        Côte-Nord
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1060" data-file-width="1885" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg/220px-Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg/330px-Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg/440px-Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mont_Tremblant_village.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mont_Tremblant_Resort" title="Mont Tremblant Resort">
          Mont Tremblant Resort
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Laurentian_Mountains" title="Laurentian Mountains">
          Laurentian Mountains
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Peninsula" title="Labrador Peninsula">
        Labrador Peninsula
       </a>
       is covered by the Laurentian Plateau (or
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">
        Canadian Shield
       </a>
       ), dotted with mountains such as
       <a href="/wiki/Otish_Mountains" title="Otish Mountains">
        Otish Mountains
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Peninsula" title="Ungava Peninsula">
        Ungava Peninsula
       </a>
       is notably composed of D'Youville mountains, Puvirnituq mountains and Pingualuit crater. While low and medium altitude peak from western Quebec to the far north, high altitudes mountains emerge in the
       <a href="/wiki/Capitale-Nationale" title="Capitale-Nationale">
        Capitale-Nationale
       </a>
       region to the extreme east, along its longitude. In the
       <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Peninsula" title="Labrador Peninsula">
        Labrador Peninsula
       </a>
       portion of the Shield, the far northern region of
       <a href="/wiki/Nunavik" title="Nunavik">
        Nunavik
       </a>
       includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Peninsula" title="Ungava Peninsula">
        Ungava Peninsula
       </a>
       and consists of flat
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">
        Arctic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">
        tundra
       </a>
       inhabited mostly by the
       <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">
        Inuit
       </a>
       . Further south lie the
       <a href="/wiki/Subarctic" title="Subarctic">
        subarctic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Canadian_Shield_taiga" title="Eastern Canadian Shield taiga">
        Eastern Canadian Shield taiga
       </a>
       ecoregion and the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        boreal forest
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Canadian_Shield_forests" title="Central Canadian Shield forests">
        Central Canadian Shield forests
       </a>
       , where
       <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">
        spruce
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">
        fir
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">
        poplar
       </a>
       trees provide raw materials for Quebec's
       <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry_in_Canada" title="Pulp and paper industry in Canada">
        pulp and paper
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">
        lumber
       </a>
       industries. Although the area is inhabited principally by the
       <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">
        Cree
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Naskapi" title="Naskapi">
        Naskapi
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Innu_people" title="Innu people">
        Innu
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">
        First Nations
       </a>
       , thousands of temporary workers reside at
       <a href="/wiki/Radisson,_Quebec" title="Radisson, Quebec">
        Radisson
       </a>
       to service the massive
       <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Project" title="James Bay Project">
        James Bay Hydroelectric Project
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/La_Grande_River" title="La Grande River">
        La Grande
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eastmain_River" title="Eastmain River">
        Eastmain
       </a>
       rivers. The southern portion of the shield extends to the
       <a href="/wiki/Laurentian_Mountains" title="Laurentian Mountains">
        Laurentians
       </a>
       , a mountain range just north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        Saint Lawrence Lowland
       </a>
       , that attracts local and international tourists to ski hills and lakeside resorts.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Chaudi%C3%A8re-Appalaches" title="Chaudière-Appalaches">
        Appalachian
       </a>
       region of Quebec has a narrow strip of ancient mountains along the southeastern border of Quebec. The
       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">
        Appalachians
       </a>
       are actually a huge chain that extends from
       <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">
        Alabama
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland
       </a>
       . In between, it covers in Quebec near 800 km (497 mi), from the Montérégie hills to the Gaspé Peninsula. In western Quebec, the average altitude is about 500 metres, while in the Gaspé Peninsula, the Appalachian peaks (especially the Chic-Choc) are among the highest in Quebec, exceeding 1000 metres.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1305" data-file-width="900" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
          Köppen climate types
         </a>
         of Quebec
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec has three main climate regions. Southern and western Quebec, including most of the major population centres, have a
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        humid continental climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       <i>
        Dfb
       </i>
       ) with four distinct seasons having warm to occasionally hot and humid summers and often very cold and snowy winters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main climatic influences are from western and northern Canada and move eastward, and from the southern and central United States that move northward. Because of the influence of both storm systems from the core of North America and the Atlantic Ocean, precipitation is abundant throughout the year, with most areas receiving more than 1,000 millimetres (39 in) of precipitation, including over 300 centimetres (120 in) of snow in many areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the summer, severe weather patterns (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">
        tornadoes
       </a>
       and severe
       <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">
        thunderstorms
       </a>
       ) occur occasionally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of central Quebec has a
       <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">
        subarctic climate
       </a>
       (Köppen
       <i>
        Dfc
       </i>
       ). Winters are long, very cold, and snowy, and among the coldest in eastern Canada, while summers are warm but very short due to the higher latitude and the greater influence of Arctic air masses. Precipitation is also somewhat less than farther south, except at some of the higher elevations. The northern regions of Quebec have an
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Arctic" title="Climate of the Arctic">
        arctic climate
       </a>
       (Köppen
       <i>
        ET
       </i>
       ), with very cold winters and short, much cooler summers. The primary influences in this region are the Arctic Ocean currents (such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Current" title="Labrador Current">
        Labrador Current
       </a>
       ) and continental air masses from the High
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">
        Arctic
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg/220px-Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg/330px-Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg/440px-Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baie_St-Paul_Hiver.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Baie-Saint-Paul" title="Baie-Saint-Paul">
          Baie-Saint-Paul
         </a>
         during winter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The four seasons in Quebec are spring, summer, autumn and winter, with conditions differing by region. They are then differentiated according to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insolation" title="Insolation">
        insolation
       </a>
       , temperature and precipitation of snow and rain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At Quebec City, the length of the daily sunshine varies from 8:37 hrs in December to 15:50 hrs in June; the annual variation is much greater (from 4:54 to 19:29 hrs) at the northern tip of the province.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From temperate zones to the northern territories of the Far North, the brightness varies with latitude, as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/Aurora" title="Aurora">
        Northern Lights
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">
        midnight sun
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is divided into four climatic zones: arctic, subarctic, humid continental and East maritime. From south to north, average temperatures range in summer between 25 and 5 °C (77 and 41 °F) and, in winter, between −10 and −25 °C (14 and −13 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In periods of intense heat and cold, temperatures can reach 35 °C (95 °F) in the summer
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatetabular_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-climatetabular-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and −40 °C (−40 °F) during the Quebec winter,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatetabular_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-climatetabular-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They may vary depending on the
       <a href="/wiki/Humidex" title="Humidex">
        Humidex
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Wind_chill" title="Wind chill">
        Wind chill
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The all-time record of the greatest precipitation in winter was established in winter 2007–2008, with more than five metres
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of snow in the area of Quebec City, while the average amount received per winter is around three metres.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       March 1971, however, saw the "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Canadian_Blizzard_of_March_1971" title="Eastern Canadian Blizzard of March 1971">
        Century's Snowstorm
       </a>
       " with more than 40 centimetres (16 in) in Montreal to 80 centimetres (31 in) in
       <a href="/wiki/RCAF_Station_Mont_Apica" title="RCAF Station Mont Apica">
        Mont Apica
       </a>
       of snow within 24 hours in many regions of southern Quebec. Also, the winter of 2010 was the warmest and driest recorded in more than 60 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">
        Wildlife
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The large land wildlife is mainly composed of the
       <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">
        white-tailed deer
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">
        moose
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Muskox" title="Muskox">
        muskox
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">
        caribou
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">
        American black bear
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">
        polar bear
       </a>
       . The average land wildlife includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">
        cougar
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">
        coyote
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_wolf" title="Eastern wolf">
        eastern wolf
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">
        bobcat
       </a>
       (wild cat), the
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_fox" title="Arctic fox">
        Arctic fox
       </a>
       , the fox, etc. The small animals seen most commonly include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_grey_squirrel" title="Eastern grey squirrel">
        eastern grey squirrel
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Snowshoe_hare" title="Snowshoe hare">
        snowshoe hare
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Groundhog" title="Groundhog">
        groundhog
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Skunk" title="Skunk">
        skunk
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">
        raccoon
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Chipmunk" title="Chipmunk">
        chipmunk
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_beaver" title="North American beaver">
        Canadian beaver
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Biodiversity of the estuary and gulf of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">
        Saint Lawrence River
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       consists of an aquatic mammal wildlife, of which most goes upriver through the estuary and the
       <a href="/wiki/Saguenay%E2%80%93St._Lawrence_Marine_Park" title="Saguenay–St. Lawrence Marine Park">
        Saguenay–St. Lawrence Marine Park
       </a>
       until the
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Île d'Orléans">
        <i>
         Île d'Orléans
        </i>
        (French for Orleans Island)
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">
        blue whale
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beluga_(whale)" title="Beluga (whale)">
        beluga
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">
        minke whale
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Harp_seal" title="Harp seal">
        harp seal
       </a>
       (earless seal). Among the Nordic marine animals, there are two particularly important to cite: the
       <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">
        walrus
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Narwhal" title="Narwhal">
        narwhal
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="811" data-file-width="1200" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg/220px-Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg/330px-Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg/440px-Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harfang_en_vol_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">
          Snowy owl
         </a>
         : official bird of Quebec
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Inland waters are populated by small to large fresh water fish, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Largemouth_bass" title="Largemouth bass">
        largemouth bass
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/American_pickerel" title="American pickerel">
        American pickerel
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">
        walleye
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Acipenser_oxyrinchus" title="Acipenser oxyrinchus">
         Acipenser oxyrinchus
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Muskellunge" title="Muskellunge">
        muskellunge
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_cod" title="Atlantic cod">
        Atlantic cod
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_char" title="Arctic char">
        Arctic char
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Brook_trout" title="Brook trout">
        brook trout
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Microgadus_tomcod" title="Microgadus tomcod">
         Microgadus tomcod
        </a>
       </i>
       (tomcod), the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_salmon" title="Atlantic salmon">
        Atlantic salmon
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">
        rainbow trout
       </a>
       , etc.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the birds commonly seen in the southern inhabited part of Quebec, there are the
       <a href="/wiki/American_robin" title="American robin">
        American robin
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/House_sparrow" title="House sparrow">
        house sparrow
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Red-winged_blackbird" title="Red-winged blackbird">
        red-winged blackbird
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mallard" title="Mallard">
        mallard
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Common_grackle" title="Common grackle">
        common grackle
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_jay" title="Blue jay">
        blue jay
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/American_crow" title="American crow">
        American crow
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Black-capped_chickadee" title="Black-capped chickadee">
        black-capped chickadee
       </a>
       , some
       <a href="/wiki/New_World_warbler" title="New World warbler">
        warblers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Swallow" title="Swallow">
        swallows
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_starling" title="European starling">
        starling
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_pigeon" title="Rock pigeon">
        rock pigeon
       </a>
       , the latter two having been introduced in Quebec and are found mainly in urban areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrûlotte2009_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrûlotte2009-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Avian fauna includes birds of prey like the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">
        golden eagle
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon">
        peregrine falcon
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">
        snowy owl
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">
        bald eagle
       </a>
       . Sea and semi-aquatic birds seen in Quebec are mostly the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_goose" title="Canada goose">
        Canada goose
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Double-crested_cormorant" title="Double-crested cormorant">
        double-crested cormorant
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_gannet" title="Northern gannet">
        northern gannet
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/European_herring_gull" title="European herring gull">
        European herring gull
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_blue_heron" title="Great blue heron">
        great blue heron
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Sandhill_crane" title="Sandhill crane">
        sandhill crane
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">
        Atlantic puffin
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Common_loon" title="Common loon">
        common loon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many more species of land, maritime or avian wildlife are seen in Quebec, but most of the Quebec-specific species and the most commonly seen species are listed above.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some livestock have the title of "Québec heritage breed", namely the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_horse" title="Canadian horse">
        Canadian horse
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chantecler_(chicken)" title="Chantecler (chicken)">
        Chantecler chicken
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadienne_cattle" title="Canadienne cattle">
        Canadian cow
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loi_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-loi-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Moreover, in addition to food certified as "organic", Charlevoix lamb is the first local Quebec product whose geographical indication is protected.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Livestock production also includes the pig breeds Landrace, Duroc and Yorkshire
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and many breeds of sheep
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and cattle.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Wildlife Foundation of Quebec and the Data Centre on Natural Heritage of Quebec (CDPNQ)(French acronym)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are the main agencies working with officers for wildlife conservation in Quebec.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetation">
        Vegetation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg/220px-Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg/330px-Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg/440px-Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gasp%C3%A9_taiga.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Taiga forest in Gaspé, Québec, Canada
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Given the geology of the province and its different climates, there is an established number of large areas of vegetation in Quebec. These areas, listed in order from the northernmost to the southernmost are: the
       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">
        tundra
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">
        Canadian boreal forest
       </a>
       (coniferous),
       <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest">
        mixed forest
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">
        deciduous forest
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On the edge of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ungava_Bay" title="Ungava Bay">
        Ungava Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Strait" title="Hudson Strait">
        Hudson Strait
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">
        tundra
       </a>
       , whose flora is limited to a low vegetation of
       <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">
        lichen
       </a>
       with only less than 50 growing days a year. The tundra vegetation survives an average annual temperature of −8 °C (18 °F). The tundra covers more than 24% of the area of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Further south, the climate is conducive to the growth of the
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">
        Canadian boreal forest
       </a>
       , bounded on the north by the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1630" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg/220px-Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg/330px-Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg/440px-Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecoregions_quebec_map.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The different forest areas of Quebec
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Not as arid as the
       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">
        tundra
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       is associated with the sub-Arctic regions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">
        Canadian Shield
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_veg_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-types_veg-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is characterized by a greater number of both plant (600) and animal (206) species, many of which live there all year. The
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       covers about 20% of the total area of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">
        Canadian boreal forest
       </a>
       is the northernmost and most abundant of the three forest areas in Quebec that straddle the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">
        Canadian Shield
       </a>
       and the upper
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        lowlands
       </a>
       of the province. Given a warmer climate, the diversity of organisms is also higher, since there are about 850 plant species and 280
       <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">
        vertebrates
       </a>
       species. The
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">
        Canadian boreal forest
       </a>
       covers 27% of the area of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_forest" title="Mixed forest">
        mixed forest
       </a>
       is a transition zone between the
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">
        Canadian boreal forest
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deciduous_forest" title="Deciduous forest">
        deciduous forest
       </a>
       . By virtue of its transient nature, this area contains a diversity of habitats resulting in large numbers of plant (1000) and
       <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">
        vertebrates
       </a>
       (350) species, despite relatively cool temperatures. The ecozone
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_forest" title="Mixed forest">
        mixed forest
       </a>
       covers 11.5% of the area of Quebec and is characteristic of the
       <a href="/wiki/Laurentides" title="Laurentides">
        Laurentians
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Chaudi%C3%A8re-Appalaches" title="Chaudière-Appalaches">
        Appalachians
       </a>
       and the eastern
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        lowlands
       </a>
       forests.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_veg_62-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-types_veg-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The third most northern forest area is characterized by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deciduous_forest" title="Deciduous forest">
        deciduous forests
       </a>
       . Because of its climate (average annual temperature of 7 °C (45 °F)), it is in this area that one finds the greatest diversity of species, including more than 1600
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" title="Vascular plants">
        vascular plants
       </a>
       and 440
       <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">
        vertebrates
       </a>
       . Its relatively long growing season lasts almost 200 days and its fertile soils make it the centre of agricultural activity and therefore of urbanization of Quebec. Most of Quebec's population lives in this area of vegetation, almost entirely along the banks of the St. Lawrence. Deciduous forests cover approximately 6.6% of the area of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturalhistory_39-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-naturalhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The total forest area of Quebec is estimated at 750,300 square kilometres (289,700 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domaine_forestier_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-domaine_forestier-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the
       <a href="/wiki/Abitibi-T%C3%A9miscamingue" title="Abitibi-Témiscamingue">
        Abitibi-Témiscamingue
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Côte-Nord">
        North Shore
       </a>
       , the forest is composed primarily of conifers such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Abies_balsamea" title="Abies balsamea">
         Abies balsamea
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_pine" title="Jack pine">
        jack pine
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Picea_glauca" title="Picea glauca">
        white spruce
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Picea_mariana" title="Picea mariana">
        black spruce
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Larix_laricina" title="Larix laricina">
        tamarack
       </a>
       . Some species of deciduous trees such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Betula_alleghaniensis" title="Betula alleghaniensis">
        yellow birch
       </a>
       appear when the river is approached in the south. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deciduous_forest" title="Deciduous forest">
        deciduous forest
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Lowlands" title="Saint Lawrence Lowlands">
        Saint Lawrence Lowlands
       </a>
       is mostly composed of deciduous species such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Acer_saccharum" title="Acer saccharum">
        sugar maple
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Acer_rubrum" title="Acer rubrum">
        red maple
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Fraxinus_americana" title="Fraxinus americana">
        white ash
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Fagus_grandifolia" title="Fagus grandifolia">
        American beech
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Juglans_cinerea" title="Juglans cinerea">
        butternut (white walnut)
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Ulmus_americana" title="Ulmus americana">
        American elm
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Tilia_americana" title="Tilia americana">
        basswood
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Carya_cordiformis" title="Carya cordiformis">
        bitternut hickory
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Quercus_rubra" title="Quercus rubra">
        northern red oak
       </a>
       as well as some conifers such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_white_pine" title="Eastern white pine">
        eastern white pine
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Thuja_occidentalis" title="Thuja occidentalis">
        northern whitecedar
       </a>
       . The distribution areas of the
       <a href="/wiki/Betula_papyrifera" title="Betula papyrifera">
        paper birch
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Populus_tremuloides" title="Populus tremuloides">
        trembling aspen
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sorbus" title="Sorbus">
        mountain ash
       </a>
       cover more than half of Quebec territory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Quebec" title="History of Quebec">
        History of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_peoples_and_European_exploration">
        Indigenous peoples and European exploration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway,_7,900_BPE.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png/220px-Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png/330px-Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png/440px-Glacial_Lake_Agassiz_and_Glacial_Lake_Ojibway%2C_7%2C900_BPE.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
