      <p>
       <small>
        <i>
         Percentages are calculated as a proportion of the total number of respondents (7,435,905).
         <br/>
         Only groups with more than 0.5 percent of respondents are shown.
        </i>
       </small>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is unique among the provinces in its overwhelmingly Roman Catholic population. This is a legacy of colonial times when only Roman Catholics were permitted to settle in
       <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">
        New France
       </a>
       . The 2001 census showed the population to be 90.3 percent Christian (in contrast to 77 percent for the whole country) with 83.4 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
        Catholic Christian
       </a>
       (including 83.2 percent Roman Catholic); 4.7 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant Christian
       </a>
       (including 1.2 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">
        Anglican
       </a>
       , 0.7 percent
       <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">
        United Church
       </a>
       ; and 0.5 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">
        Baptist
       </a>
       ); 1.4 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">
        Orthodox Christian
       </a>
       (including 0.7 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox" title="Greek Orthodox">
        Greek Orthodox
       </a>
       ); and 0.8 percent other Christian; as well as 1.5 percent Muslim; 1.3 percent Jewish; 0.6 percent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">
        Buddhist
       </a>
       ; 0.3 percent
       <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
        Hindu
       </a>
       ; and 0.1 percent
       <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">
        Sikh
       </a>
       . An additional 5.8 percent of the population said they had no religious affiliation (including 5.6 percent who stated that they had no religion at all).
       <br/>
       <small>
        <i>
         Percentages are calculated as a proportion of the total number of respondents (7,125,580)
        </i>
       </small>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Language_demographics_of_Quebec" title="Language demographics of Quebec">
        Language demographics of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1649" data-file-width="3653" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg/220px-D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg/330px-D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg/440px-D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9bat_sur_les_langues_lors_de_la_premi%C3%A8re_Assembl%C3%A9e_l%C3%A9gislative_du_Bas-Canada_le_21_janvier_1793.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         This image shows the painting Débat sur les langues lors de la première Assemblée législative du Bas-Canada le 21 janvier 1793 (Debate on languages during the first Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada, January 21, 1793), by
         <a href="/wiki/Charles_Huot" title="Charles Huot">
          Charles Huot
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_langues.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3745" data-file-width="3311" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Quebec_langues.png/220px-Quebec_langues.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Quebec_langues.png/330px-Quebec_langues.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Quebec_langues.png/440px-Quebec_langues.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_langues.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <table align="center" style="width:100%; vertical-align:top; border:1px solid #ABD5F5; background-color:#F1F5FC; margin-top:2px;">
          <tr>
           <td>
            <div style="text-align:center">
             Linguistic map of the province of Quebec (source: Statistics Canada, 2006 census)
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Francophone majority, less than 33% Anglophone
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Francophone majority, more than 33% Anglophone
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Anglophone majority, less than 33% Francophone
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Anglophone majority, more than 33% Francophone
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:brown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Allophone majority (indigenous)
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             Data not available
            </div>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       of Quebec is French. Quebec is the only Canadian province whose population is mainly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">
        Francophone
       </a>
       ; 6,102,210 people (78.1 percent of the population) recorded it as their sole native language in the 2011 Census, and 6,249,085 (80.0%) recorded that they spoke it most often at home.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Knowledge of French is widespread even among those who do not speak it natively; in 2011, about 94.4 percent of the total population reported being able to speak French, alone or in combination with other languages, while 47.3% reported being able to speak English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, 599,230 people (7.7 percent of the population) people in Quebec declared English to be their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" title="Mother tongue">
        mother tongue
       </a>
       , and 767,415 (9.8 percent) used it most often as their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_language" title="Home language">
        home language
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_Quebecers" title="English-speaking Quebecers">
        English-speaking community
       </a>
       or Anglophones are entitled to services in English in the areas of justice, health, and education;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charteroffrench_136-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-charteroffrench-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       services in English are offered in municipalities in which more than half the residents have English as their mother tongue.
       <a href="/wiki/Allophone_(Quebec)" title="Allophone (Quebec)">
        Allophones
       </a>
       , people whose mother tongue is neither French nor English, made up 12.3 percent (961,700) of the population, according to the 2011 census, though a smaller figure – 554,400 (7.1 percent) – actually used these languages most often in the home.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A considerable number of Quebec residents consider themselves to be
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingual" title="Bilingual">
        bilingual
       </a>
       in French and English. In Quebec, about 42.6 percent of the population (3,328,725 people) report knowing both languages; this is the highest proportion of bilinguals of any Canadian province.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One specific area in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bilingual_belt" title="Bilingual belt">
        Bilingual Belt
       </a>
       called the West Island of Montreal, represented by the federal electoral district of
       <a href="/wiki/Lac-Saint-Louis_(electoral_district)" title="Lac-Saint-Louis (electoral district)">
        Lac-Saint-Louis
       </a>
       , is the most bilingual area in the province: 72.8% of its residents claim to know English and French according to the most recent census.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In contrast, in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_of_Canada" title="Rest of Canada">
        rest of Canada
       </a>
       , in 2006 only about 10.2 percent (2,430,990) of the population had a knowledge of both of the country's official languages. Altogether, 17.5% of Canadians are bilingual in French and English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, the most common mother tongue languages in the province were as follows: (
       <i>
        Figures shown are for single-language responses only
       </i>
       .)
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable">
       <caption>
        Mother tongue language (2011)
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Language
        </th>
        <th>
         Number of
         <br/>
         native speakers
        </th>
        <th>
         Percentage of
         <br/>
         singular responses
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Quebec_French" title="Quebec French">
          French
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         6,102,210
        </td>
        <td>
         78%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Quebec_English" title="Quebec English">
          English
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         599,230
        </td>
        <td>
         7.7%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
          Arabic
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         164,390
        </td>
        <td>
         2%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
          Spanish
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         141,000
        </td>
        <td>
         1.8%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
          Italian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         121,720
        </td>
        <td>
         1.6%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Following were
       <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">
        Creoles
       </a>
       (0.8%), Chinese (0.6%), Greek (0.5%), Portuguese (0.5%), Romanian (0.4%), Vietnamese (0.3%), and Russian (0.3%). In addition, 152,820 (2.0%) reported having more than one native language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www12.statcan.gc.ca_135-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-www12.statcan.gc.ca-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       English is not designated an official language by
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_law" title="Quebec law">
        Quebec law
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charteroffrench_136-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-charteroffrench-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, both English and French are required by the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1867" title="Constitution Act, 1867">
         Constitution Act, 1867
        </a>
       </i>
       for the enactment of laws and regulations and any person may use English or French in the National Assembly and the courts of Quebec. The books and records of the National Assembly must also be kept in both languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Until 1969, Quebec was the only officially bilingual province in Canada and most public institutions functioned in both languages. English was also used in the legislature, government commissions and courts.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the 1970s, languages other than French on commercial signs have been permitted only if French is given marked prominence. This law has been the subject of periodic controversy since its inception. The written forms of French place-names in Canada retain their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_diacritics" title="French diacritics">
        diacritics
       </a>
       such as accent marks over vowels in English text. Legitimate exceptions are
       <b>
        Montreal
       </b>
       and
       <b>
        Quebec
       </b>
       . However, the accented forms are increasingly evident in some publications. The
       <i>
        Canadian Style
       </i>
       states that
       <b>
        Montréal
       </b>
       and
       <b>
        Québec
       </b>
       (the city) must retain their accents in English federal documents.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_centres">
        Population centres
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

        List of population centres in Quebec
       </a>
      </div>

           [140]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th style="text-align:center;background:#f8f8f16;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_100_largest_metropolitan_areas_in_Canada" title="List of the 100 largest metropolitan areas in Canada">
          Rank
         </a>
        </th>
        <th style="text-align:center;background:#f5f5f5;">
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Canada" title="List of cities in Canada">
          Core City

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Quebec" title="Economy of Quebec">
        Economy of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec has an
       <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">
        advanced
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">
        market-based
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">
        open economy
       </a>
       . In 2009, its gross domestic product (GDP) of US$32,408 per capita at
       <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
        purchasing power parity
       </a>
       puts the province at par with Japan, Italy and Spain, but remains lower than the Canadian average of US$37,830 per capita.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Template:Harvard_citation_documentation#Wikilink_to_citation_does_not_work" title="Template:Harvard citation documentation">
          <span title="Template:Harvard citation documentation#Wikilink to citation does not work">
           citation not found
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The economy of Quebec is ranked the 37th largest economy in the world just behind
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       and 28th for the gross domestic product (GDP) per capita.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2724" data-file-width="9017" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg/300px-Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg/450px-Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg/600px-Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montreal_Twilight_Panorama_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of
         <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
          Montreal
         </a>
         from the Mont-Royal belvedere
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The economy of Quebec represents 20.36% of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by gross domestic product">
        total GDP of Canada
       </a>
       . Like most industrialized countries, the economy of Quebec is based mainly on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Services_sector" title="Services sector">
        services sector
       </a>
       . Quebec's economy has traditionally been fuelled by abundant natural resources, a well-developed infrastructure, and average productivity. The provincial GDP in 2010 was C$319,348 billion,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grossdomestic2010_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Grossdomestic2010-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which makes Quebec the second largest economy in Canada.
      </p>
      <p>
       The provincial
       <a href="/wiki/Debt-to-GDP_ratio" title="Debt-to-GDP ratio">
        debt-to-GDP ratio
       </a>
       peaked at 50% in
       <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">
        fiscal year
       </a>
       2014-2015, and is projected to decline to 40% in 2021-2022.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">
        credit rating
       </a>
       of Quebec is currently
       <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">
        Aa2
       </a>
       according to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moody%27s" title="Moody's">
        Moody's
       </a>
       agency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aa2_146-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aa2-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In June 2017
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        S&amp;P
       </a>
       rated Quebec as an AA- credit risk, surpassing Ontario for the first time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4220" data-file-width="4992" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg/220px-Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg/330px-Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg/440px-Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edifice_quebec_INRS.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Institut_national_de_la_recherche_scientifique" title="Institut national de la recherche scientifique">
          Institut national de la recherche scientifique
         </a>
         helping to advance scientific knowledge and to train a new generation of students in various scientific and technological sectors. More than one million Quebecers work in the field of science and technology which represents more than 30% of Quebec's GDP.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec's economy has undergone tremendous changes over the last decade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Firmly grounded in the
       <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">
        knowledge economy
       </a>
       , Quebec has one of the highest growth rate of gross domestic product (GDP) in Canada. The knowledge sector represents about 30.9% of Quebec's GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec is experiencing faster growth of its R&amp;D spending than other Canadian provinces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec's spending in R&amp;D in 2011 was equal to 2.63% of GDP, above the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       average of 1.84% and will have to reaches the target of devoting 3% of GDP to research and development activities in 2013 according to the
       <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Strategy" title="Lisbon Strategy">
        Lisbon Strategy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The percentage spent on research and technology (R&amp;D) is the highest in Canada and higher than the averages for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G7" title="G7">
        G7
       </a>
       countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 1.1 million Quebecers work in the field of science and technology.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R&amp;D_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-R&amp;D-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1678" data-file-width="2424" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg/220px-Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg/330px-Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg/440px-Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bombardier_CSeries_mockup.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A mockup of a
         <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_CSeries" title="Bombardier CSeries">
          Bombardier CSeries
         </a>
         being developed by
         <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" title="Bombardier Aerospace">
          Bombardier Aerospace
         </a>
         . Since 1856, Quebec has established itself as a pioneer of modern aerospace industry.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
          <a href="#cite_note-154">
           [154]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Quebec has over 260 companies which employ about 43,000 people. Approximately 62% of the Canadian aerospace industry is based in Quebec.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
          <a href="#cite_note-155">
           [155]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
          <a href="#cite_note-156">
           [156]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec is also a major player in several leading-edge industries including
       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">
        aerospace
       </a>
       , information technologies and software and
       <a href="/wiki/Multimedia" title="Multimedia">
        multimedia
       </a>
       . Approximately 60% of the production of the Canadian aerospace industry are from Quebec, where sales totalled C$12.4 billion in 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec is one of North America's leading high-tech player. This vast sector encompassing approximately 7,300 businesses and employ more than 145,000 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Marois" title="Pauline Marois">
        Pauline Marois
       </a>
       has recently unveiled a two billion dollar budget for the period between 2013 to 2017 to create about 115,000 new jobs in knowledge and innovation sectors. The government promises to provide about 3% of Quebec's GDP in research and development (R&amp;D).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Approximately 180 000 Quebeckers are currently working in different field of
       <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">
        information technology
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 52% of Canadian companies in these sectors are based in Quebec, mainly in Montreal and Quebec City. There are currently approximately 115 telecommunications companies established in the province, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">
        Motorola
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">
        Ericsson
       </a>
       . About 60 000 people currently working in computer software development. Approximately 12 900 people working in over 110 companies such as
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       , CMC, and
       <a href="/wiki/Matrox" title="Matrox">
        Matrox
       </a>
       . The multimedia sector is also dominated by the province of Quebec. Several companies, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">
        Ubisoft
       </a>
       settled in Quebec since the late 1990s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The mining industry accounted for approximately 6.3% of Quebec's GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It employs approximately 50,000 people
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amq-inc_163-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-amq-inc-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 158 different companies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amq-inc_163-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-amq-inc-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The pulp and paper industries generate annual shipments valued at more than $14 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The forest products industry ranks second in exports, with shipments valued at almost $11 billion. It is also the main, and in some circumstances only, source of manufacturing activity in more than 250 municipalities in the province. The forest industry has slowed in recent years because of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_%E2%80%93_Canada_softwood_lumber_dispute" title="United States – Canada softwood lumber dispute">
        softwood lumber dispute
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This industry employs 68,000 people in several regions of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This industry accounted for 3.1% of Quebec's GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Agri-food industry plays an important role in the economy of Quebec. It accounts for 8% of the Quebec's GDP and generate $19.2 billion. This industry generated 487,000 jobs in agriculture, fisheries, manufacturing of food, beverages and tobacco and food distribution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">
        Natural resources
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fermont.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Fermont.JPG/220px-Fermont.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Fermont.JPG/330px-Fermont.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Fermont.JPG/440px-Fermont.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fermont.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mining town of
         <a href="/wiki/Fermont" title="Fermont">
          Fermont
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Côte-Nord">
          North Shore
         </a>
         , the beginning of the road of iron.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The abundance of natural resources gives Quebec an advantageous position on the world market. Quebec stands out particularly in the mining sector, ranking among the top ten areas to do business in mining.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It also stands for the exploitation of its forest resources.
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is remarkable for the natural resources of its vast territory. It has about 30 mines, 158 exploration companies and fifteen primary processing industries. Many metallic minerals are exploited, the principals are gold, iron, copper and
       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">
        zinc
       </a>
       . Many other substances are extracted including
       <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">
        titanium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Asbestos" title="Asbestos">
        asbestos
       </a>
       , silver,
       <a href="/wiki/Magnesium" title="Magnesium">
        magnesium
       </a>
       , nickel and many other metals and industrial minerals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, only 40% of the mineral potential of Quebec is currently known. In 2003, the value of mineral exploitation reached Quebec 3.7 billion Canadian dollars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Moreover, as a major centre of exploration for diamonds,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec has seen, since 2002, an increase in its mineral explorations, particularly in the Northwest as well as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Otish_Mountains" title="Otish Mountains">
        Otish Mountains
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Torngat_Mountains" title="Torngat Mountains">
        Torngat Mountains
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The vast majority (90.5%) of Quebec's forests are publicly owned. Forests cover more than half of Quebec's territory, for a total area of nearly 761,100 square kilometres (293,900 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
        <a href="#cite_note-173">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Quebec forest area covers seven degrees of latitude.
      </p>
      <p>
       More than a million lakes and rivers cover Quebec, occupying 21% of the total area of its territory. The aquatic environment is composed of 12.1% of fresh water and 9.2% of saltwater (percentage of total QC area).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">
        Science and technology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg/220px-Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg/330px-Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg/440px-Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prof._Dr._Rudolph_A._Marcus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_A._Marcus" title="Rudolph A. Marcus">
          Rudolph A. Marcus
         </a>
         , chemist and
         <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">
          Nobel Prize in Chemistry
         </a>
         laureate.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
          <a href="#cite_note-175">
           [175]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2229" data-file-width="2480" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg/220px-Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg/330px-Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg/440px-Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_Lunar_Module_Eagle_in_landing_configuration_in_lunar_orbit_from_the_Command_and_Service_Module_Columbia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         In 1969,
         <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9roux-Devtek" title="Héroux-Devtek">
          Héroux-Devtek
         </a>
         Has designed and manufactured the
         <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">
          undercarriage
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
          Apollo Lunar Module
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The government of Quebec has launched the Stratégie québécoise de la recherche et de l'innovation (SQRI) in 2007 which aims to promote development through research, science and technology. The government hopes to create a strong culture of innovation in Quebec for the next decades and to create a sustainable economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SQRI_176-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SQRI-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The spending on research and development reached some 7.824 billion dollars in 2007, roughly the equivalent of 2.63% of Quebec's GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SQRI_176-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-SQRI-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec is ranked, as of March 2011, 13th in the world in terms of investment in research and development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The research and development expenditures will be more than 3% of the province's GDP in 2013. The R&amp;D expenditure in Quebec is higher than the average
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G7" title="G7">
        G7
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">
        OECD
       </a>
       countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R&amp;D_153-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-R&amp;D-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Science and technology are key factors in the economic position of Quebec. More than one million people in Quebec are employed in the science and technology sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R&amp;D_153-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-R&amp;D-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is considered as one of world leaders in
       <a href="/wiki/Basic_research" title="Basic research">
        fundamental scientific research
       </a>
       , having produced ten
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">
        Nobel laureates
       </a>
       in either physics, chemistry, or medicine.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is also considered as one of the world leaders in sectors such as aerospace, information technology, biotechnology and pharmaceuticals, and therefore plays a significant role in the world's scientific and technological communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
        <a href="#cite_note-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec is also active in the development of its energy industries, including
       <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
        renewable energy
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">
        hydropower
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">
        wind power
       </a>
       . Quebec has had over 9,469 scientific publications in the sector of medicine, biomedical research and engineering since the year 2000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
        <a href="#cite_note-180">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Overall, the province of Quebec count about 125 scientific publications per 100,000 inhabitants in 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The contribution of Quebec in science and technology represent approximately 1% of the researches worldwide since the 1980s to 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Between 1991 to 2000, Quebec produced more scientific papers per 100,000 inhabitants than the United States and Germany.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">
        Canadian Space Agency
       </a>
       was established in Quebec due to its major role in this research field. A total of three Quebecers have been in space since the creation of the CSA:
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Garneau" title="Marc Garneau">
        Marc Garneau
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Julie_Payette" title="Julie Payette">
        Julie Payette
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guy_Lalibert%C3%A9" title="Guy Laliberté">
        Guy Laliberté
       </a>
       . Quebec has also contributed to the creation of some Canadian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_satellite" title="Artificial satellite">
        artificial satellites
       </a>
       including
       <a href="/wiki/SCISAT-1" title="SCISAT-1">
        SCISAT-1
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/ISIS_(satellite)" title="ISIS (satellite)">
        ISIS
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Radarsat-1" title="Radarsat-1">
        Radarsat-1
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Radarsat-2" title="Radarsat-2">
        Radarsat-2
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
        <a href="#cite_note-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
        <a href="#cite_note-186">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The province is one of the world leaders in the field of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_science" title="Space science">
        space science
       </a>
       and contributed to important discoveries in this field.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
        <a href="#cite_note-187">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the most recent is the discovery of the complex
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">
        extrasolar planets
       </a>
       system
       <a href="/wiki/HR_8799" title="HR 8799">
        HR 8799
       </a>
       . HR 8799 is the first direct observation of an exoplanet in history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
        <a href="#cite_note-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Olivier Daigle and Claude Carignan, astrophysicists from
       <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Université de Montréal">
        Université de Montréal
       </a>
       have invented an astronomical camera approximately 500 times more powerful than those currently on the market.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is therefore considered as the most sensitive camera in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
        <a href="#cite_note-192">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Mont_M%C3%A9gantic_Observatory" title="Mont Mégantic Observatory">
        Mont Mégantic Observatory
       </a>
       was recently equipped with this camera.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
        <a href="#cite_note-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec ranks among the world leaders in the field of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_science" title="Life science">
        life science
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emergex_195-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-emergex-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">
        William Osler
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wilder_Penfield" title="Wilder Penfield">
        Wilder Penfield
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donald_Olding_Hebb" title="Donald Olding Hebb">
        Donald Hebb
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Milner" title="Brenda Milner">
        Brenda Milner
       </a>
       , and others made significant discoveries in
       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">
        medicine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">
        neuroscience
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">
        psychology
       </a>
       while working at
       <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">
        McGill University
       </a>
       in Montreal. Quebec has more than 450 biotechnology and pharmaceutical companies which together employ more than 25,000 people and 10,000 highly qualified researchers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emergex_195-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-emergex-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Montreal is ranked 4th in North America for the number of jobs in the pharmaceutical sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emergex_195-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-emergex-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
        <a href="#cite_note-196">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cmarcoux3.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cmarcoux3.JPG/220px-Cmarcoux3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cmarcoux3.JPG/330px-Cmarcoux3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cmarcoux3.JPG/440px-Cmarcoux3.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cmarcoux3.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The ferry N.M.
         <i>
          Camille-Marcoux
         </i>
         , of the
         <i>
          Société des traversiers du Québec
         </i>
         , ensuring liaison Baie-Comeau—Matane and Godbout—Matane.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Development and security of land transportation in Canada are provided by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minist%C3%A8re_des_Transports_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Ministère des Transports du Québec">
        ministère des Transports du Québec
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
        <a href="#cite_note-197">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other organizations, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Coast_Guard" title="Canadian Coast Guard">
        Canadian Coast Guard
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nav_Canada" title="Nav Canada">
        Nav Canada
       </a>
       , provide the same service for the sea and air transportation. The
       <i>
        Commission des transports du Québec
       </i>
       works with the freight carriers and the public transport.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        réseau routier québécois
       </i>
       (Quebec road network) is managed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_de_l%27assurance_automobile_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Société de l'assurance automobile du Québec">
        Société de l'assurance automobile du Québec
       </a>
       (SAAQ) (Quebec Automobile Insurance Corporation) and consists of about 185,000 kilometres (115,000 mi) of highways and national, regional, local, collector and forest roads. In addition, Quebec has almost 12,000 bridges, tunnels, retaining walls, culverts and other structures
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Bridge" title="Quebec Bridge">
        Quebec Bridge
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Laviolette_Bridge" title="Laviolette Bridge">
        Laviolette Bridge
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Hippolyte_Lafontaine_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Louis-Hippolyte Lafontaine Bridge-Tunnel">
        Louis-Hippolyte Lafontaine Bridge-Tunnel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the waters of the St. Lawrence there are eight deep-water ports for the transhipment of goods. In 2003, 3886 cargo and 9.7 million tonnes of goods transited the Quebec portion of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Seaway" title="St. Lawrence Seaway">
        St. Lawrence Seaway
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transport-qc_199-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-transport-qc-199">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Concerning rail transport, Quebec has 6,678 kilometres (4,150 mi) of railways
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
       integrated in the large North American network. Although primarily intended for the transport of goods through companies such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_National" title="Canadian National">
        Canadian National
       </a>
       (CN) and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific" title="Canadian Pacific">
        Canadian Pacific
       </a>
       (CP), the Quebec railway network is also used by inter-city passengers via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Via_Rail_Canada" title="Via Rail Canada">
        Via Rail Canada
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       . In April 2012, plans were unveiled for the construction of an 800 km (497 mi) railway running north from
       <a href="/wiki/Sept-%C3%8Eles,_Quebec" title="Sept-Îles, Quebec">
        Sept-Îles
       </a>
       , to support mining and other resource extraction in the Labrador Trough.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The upper air network includes 43 airports that offer scheduled services on a daily basis.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transport-qc_199-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-transport-qc-199">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, the Government of Quebec owns airports and heliports to increase the accessibility of local services to communities in the
       <a href="/wiki/Basse-C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Basse-Côte-Nord">
        Basse-Côte-Nord
       </a>
       and northern regions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Various other transport networks crisscross the province of Quebec, including hiking trails, snowmobile trails and bike paths; the
       <a href="/wiki/Route_Verte" title="Route Verte">
        Green Road
       </a>
       being the largest with nearly 4,000 kilometres (2,500 mi) in length.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">
        Energy
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_generating_stations_in_Quebec" title="List of generating stations in Quebec">
        List of generating stations in Quebec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Hydro-Québec">
        Hydro-Québec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec has been described as a potential clean
       <a href="/wiki/Energy_superpower" title="Energy superpower">
        energy superpower
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The energy balance of Quebec has undergone a large shift over the past 30 years. In 2008, electricity ranked as the main form of energy used in Quebec (41.6%), followed by oil (38.2%) and natural gas (10.7%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
        <a href="#cite_note-206">
         [206]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec is the fourth largest producer of hydroelectricity in the world after China, Brazil and the United States and relies almost exclusively (96% in 2008) on this source of
       <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
        renewable energy
       </a>
       for its electricity needs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
        <a href="#cite_note-207">
         [207]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Quebec" title="Culture of Quebec">
        Culture of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quebec is at the centre of French-speaking culture in North America. Its culture is a symbol of a distinct perspective.
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_nationalism" title="Quebec nationalism">
        Quebec nationalism
       </a>
       has been one expression of this perspective. Quebec's culture blends its historic roots with its aboriginal heritage and the contributions of recent immigrants, as well as receiving a strong influence from English-speaking North America.
      </p>
      <p>
       Montreal's cabarets rose to the forefront of the city's cultural life during the
       <a href="/wiki/Prohibition" title="Prohibition">
        Prohibition
       </a>
       era of Canada and the United States in the 1920s. The cabarets radically transformed the artistic scene, greatly influencing the live entertainment industry of Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
        <a href="#cite_note-208">
         [208]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Quartier_Latin,_Montreal" title="Quartier Latin, Montreal">
        Quartier Latin
       </a>
       (English: Latin Quarter) of Montreal, and Vieux-Québec (English:
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Quebec" title="Old Quebec">
        Old Quebec
       </a>
       ) in Quebec City, are two hubs of activity for today's artists. Life in the cafés and "terrasses" (outdoor restaurant terraces) reveals a Latin influence in Quebec's culture, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_Saint-Denis" title="Théâtre Saint-Denis">
        théâtre Saint-Denis
       </a>
       in Montréal and the
       <a href="/wiki/Capitole_de_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Capitole de Québec">
        Capitole de Québec
       </a>
       theatre in Quebec City being among the principal attractions.
      </p>
      <p>
       A number of governmental and non-government organizations support cultural activity in Quebec. The
       <a href="/wiki/Conseil_des_arts_et_des_lettres_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Conseil des arts et des lettres du Québec">
        Conseil des arts et des lettres du Québec
       </a>
       (CALQ) is an initiative of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_and_Communications_(Quebec)" title="Ministry of Culture and Communications (Quebec)">
        Ministry of Culture and Communications (Quebec)
       </a>
       . It supports creation, innovation, production, and international exhibits for all cultural fields of Quebec. The
       <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_de_d%C3%A9veloppement_des_entreprises_culturelles" title="Société de développement des entreprises culturelles">
        Société de développement des entreprises culturelles
       </a>
       (SODEC) works to promote and fund individuals working in the cultural industry. The
       <a href="/wiki/Prix_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Prix du Québec">
        Prix du Québec
       </a>
       is an award given by the government to confer the highest distinction and honour to individuals demonstrating exceptional achievement in their respective cultural field.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Society">
        Society
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On February 8, 2007, Quebec Premier
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Charest" title="Jean Charest">
        Jean Charest
       </a>
       announced the setting up of a
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bouchard-Taylor_Commission" title="Bouchard-Taylor Commission">
         Commission tasked with consulting Quebec Society on the matter of arrangements regarding cultural diversity
        </a>
       </i>
       . The Premier's press release
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d'étude_209-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-d'étude-209">
         [209]
        </a>
       </sup>
       reasserted the three fundamental values of Quebec society:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        Equality between men and women, primacy of the French language, and
        <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">
         separation of church and state
        </a>
        constitute the fundamental values. They are not subject to any arrangement. They cannot be subordinated by any other principle.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d'étude_209-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-d'étude-209">
          [209]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       Furthermore, Quebec is a free and democratic society that abides by the
       <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">
        rule of law
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
        <a href="#cite_note-210">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec society bases its cohesion and specificity on a set of statements, a few notable examples of which include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_of_Human_Rights_and_Freedoms" title="Charter of Human Rights and Freedoms">
          Quebec Charter of Human Rights and Freedoms
         </a>
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
         <a href="#cite_note-211">
          [211]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_French_Language" title="Charter of the French Language">
          Charter of the French Language
         </a>
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
         <a href="#cite_note-212">
          [212]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Civil_Code_of_Quebec" title="Civil Code of Quebec">
          Civil Code of Quebec
         </a>
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
         <a href="#cite_note-213">
          [213]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">
        Music and dance
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Quebec" title="Music of Quebec">
        Music of Quebec
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dance_of_Quebec" title="Dance of Quebec">
        Dance of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Traditional music is imbued with many dances, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jig" title="Jig">
        jig
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Quadrille" title="Quadrille">
        quadrille
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Reel_(dance)" title="Reel (dance)">
        reel
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Line_dancing" title="Line dancing">
        line dancing
       </a>
       , which developed in the festivities since the early days of colonization. Various instruments are more popular in Quebec's culture: harmonica (music-of-mouth or lip-destruction),
       <a href="/wiki/Fiddle" title="Fiddle">
        fiddle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spoon_(musical_instrument)" title="Spoon (musical instrument)">
        spoons
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaw_harp" title="Jaw harp">
        jaw harp
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Accordion" title="Accordion">
        accordion
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        podorythmie
       </i>
       is a characteristic of traditional Quebec music and means giving the rhythm with the feet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
        <a href="#cite_note-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quebec traditional music is currently provided by various contemporary groups seen mostly during Christmas and New Year's Eve celebrations,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Holiday_(Quebec)" title="National Holiday (Quebec)">
        Quebec National Holiday
       </a>
       and many local festivals.
      </p>
      <p>
       Being a modern cosmopolitan society, today, all types of music can be found in Quebec. From
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">
        folk music
       </a>
       to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip-hop" title="Hip-hop">
        hip-hop
       </a>
       , music has always played an important role in Quebercers culture. From
       <a href="/wiki/La_Bolduc" title="La Bolduc">
        La Bolduc
       </a>
       in the 1920s–1930s to the contemporary artists, the music in Quebec has announced multiple songwriters and performers, pop singers and crooners, music groups and many more. Quebec's most popular artists of the last century include the singers
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Leclerc" title="Félix Leclerc">
        Félix Leclerc
       </a>
       (1950s),
       <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Vigneault" title="Gilles Vigneault">
        Gilles Vigneault
       </a>
       (1960s–present),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kate_and_Anna_McGarrigle" title="Kate and Anna McGarrigle">
        Kate and Anna McGarrigle
       </a>
       (1970s–present) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_Dion" title="Céline Dion">
        Céline Dion
       </a>
       (1980s–present).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
        <a href="#cite_note-215">
         [215]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">
        First Nations
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">
        Inuit
       </a>
       of Quebec also have their own traditional music.
      </p>
      <p>
       From Quebec's musical repertoire, the song
       <i>
        A La Claire Fontaine
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
        <a href="#cite_note-216">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was the anthem of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">
        New France
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Patriote_movement" title="Patriote movement">
        Patriots
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">
        French Canadian
       </a>
       , then replaced by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/O_Canada" title="O Canada">
         O Canada
        </a>
       </i>
       . Currently, the song
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gens_du_pays" title="Gens du pays">
         Gens du pays
        </a>
       </i>
       is by far preferred by many Quebecers to be the national anthem of Quebec. The
       <a href="/wiki/ADISQ" title="ADISQ">
        Association québécoise de l'industrie du disque, du spectacle et de la vidéo
       </a>
       (ADISQ) was created in 1978 to promote the music industry in Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
        <a href="#cite_note-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchestre_symphonique_de_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Orchestre symphonique de Québec">
        Orchestre symphonique de Québec
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchestre_symphonique_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Orchestre symphonique de Montréal">
        Orchestre symphonique de Montréal
       </a>
       are respectively associated with the Opéra de Québec and the Opéra de Montreal whose performances are presented at the
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Grand Théâtre de Québec">
        Grand Théâtre de Québec
       </a>
       and at
       <a href="/wiki/Place_des_Arts" title="Place des Arts">
        Place des Arts
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        Ballets Jazz de Montreal
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Grands Ballets
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/La_La_La_Human_Steps" title="La La La Human Steps">
        La La La Human Steps
       </a>
       are three important professional troupes of
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_dance" title="Contemporary dance">
        contemporary dance
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Film.2C_television.2C_and_radio">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Film,_television,_and_radio">
        Film, television, and radio
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Quebec" title="Cinema of Quebec">
        Cinema of Quebec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Quebec" title="Television in Quebec">
        Television in Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cin%C3%A9math%C3%A8que_qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9coise" title="Cinémathèque québécoise">
        Cinémathèque québécoise
       </a>
       has a mandate to promote the film and television heritage of Quebec. Similarly, the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Board_of_Canada" title="National Film Board of Canada">
        National Film Board of Canada
       </a>
       (NFB), a federal Crown corporation, provides for the same mission in Canada. In a similar way, the Association of Film and Television in Quebec (APFTQ) promotes independent production in film and television.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
        <a href="#cite_note-218">
         [218]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the Association of Producers and Directors of Quebec (APDQ) represents the business of filmmaking and television, the Association of Community Radio Broadcasters of Quebec (ARCQ) (French acronym) represents the independent radio stations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         [219]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several movie theatres across Quebec ensure the dissemination of Quebec cinema. With its cinematic installations, such as the
       <i>
        Cité du cinéma
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Mel's
       </i>
       studios, the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       is home to the filming of various productions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
        <a href="#cite_note-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The State corporation
       <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9l%C3%A9-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Télé-Québec">
        Télé-Québec
       </a>
       , the federal Crown corporation
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">
        CBC
       </a>
       , general and specialized private channels, networks, independent and community radio stations broadcast the various
       <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9l%C3%A9roman" title="Téléroman">
        Quebec téléromans
       </a>
       , the national and regional news, interactive and spoken programmations, etc.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
        <a href="#cite_note-221">
         [221]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
        <a href="#cite_note-222">
         [222]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Les_Rendez-vous_du_cin%C3%A9ma_qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Les Rendez-vous du cinéma québécois">
        Les Rendez-vous du cinéma québécois
       </a>
       is a festival surrounding the ceremony of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jutra_Award" title="Jutra Award">
        Jutra Awards Night
       </a>
       that rewards work and personalities of Quebec cinema.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
        <a href="#cite_note-223">
         [223]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Artis and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gemini_Awards" title="Gemini Awards">
        Gemini Awards
       </a>
       gala recognize the personalities of television and radio industry in Quebec and French Canada. The
       <i>
        Film Festival of the 3 Americas
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
        Quebec City
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        Festival of International Short Film
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saguenay,_Quebec" title="Saguenay, Quebec">
        Saguenay
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_World_Film_Festival" title="Montreal World Film Festival">
        World Film Festival
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festival_du_Nouveau_Cin%C3%A9ma" title="Festival du Nouveau Cinéma">
        Festival of New Cinema
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       , are other annual events surrounding the film industry in Quebec.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_theatre">
        Literature and theatre
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literature_of_Quebec" title="Literature of Quebec">
        Literature of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       From New France, Quebec literature was first developed in the travel accounts of explorers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">
        Jacques Cartier
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Br%C3%A9beuf" title="Jean de Brébeuf">
        Jean de Brébeuf
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Louis-Armand_de_Lom_d%27Arce_de_Lahontan,_Baron_de_Lahontan" title="Louis-Armand de Lom d'Arce de Lahontan, Baron de Lahontan">
        Baron de La Hontan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Perrot" title="Nicolas Perrot">
        Nicolas Perrot
       </a>
       , describing their relations with
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
        indigenous peoples
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        Moulin à paroles
       </i>
       traces the great texts that have shaped the history of Quebec since its foundation in 1534 until the era of modernity. The first to write the history of Quebec, since its discovery, was the historian
       <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Xavier_Garneau" title="François-Xavier Garneau">
        François-Xavier Garneau
       </a>
       . This author will be part of the current of patriotic literature (also known as the "poets of the country" and literary identity) that will arise after the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada_Rebellion" title="Lower Canada Rebellion">
        Patriots Rebellion
       </a>
       of 1837–1838.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
        <a href="#cite_note-224">
         [224]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Various tales and stories are told through oral tradition, such as, among many more, the legends of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bogeyman" title="Bogeyman">
         Bogeyman
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chasse-galerie" title="Chasse-galerie">
         Chasse-galerie
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Black Horse of Trois-Pistoles
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Complainte de Cadieux
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Marie-Josephte_Corriveau" title="Marie-Josephte Corriveau">
         Corriveau
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        dancing devil of Saint-Ambroise
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_Beaupr%C3%A9" title="Édouard Beaupré">
         Giant Beaupré
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        monsters of the lakes
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pohenegamook" title="Lake Pohenegamook">
         Pohénégamook
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Memphremagog" title="Lake Memphremagog">
         Memphremagog
        </a>
       </i>
       , of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Bridge" title="Quebec Bridge">
         Quebec Bridge
        </a>
       </i>
       (called the Devil's Bridge), the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocher_Perc%C3%A9" title="Rocher Percé">
