         Rocher Percé
        </a>
       </i>
       and of
       <i>
        Rose Latulipe
       </i>
       , for example.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDupont2008_225-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDupont2008-225">
         [225]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Quebec_writers" title="List of Quebec writers">
        Quebec poets
       </a>
       and prominent authors marked their era and today remain anchored in the collective imagination, like, among others, Philippe Aubert de Gaspé,
       <a href="/wiki/Octave_Cr%C3%A9mazie" title="Octave Crémazie">
        Octave Crémazie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Honor%C3%A9_Beaugrand" title="Honoré Beaugrand">
        Honoré Beaugrand
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Nelligan" title="Émile Nelligan">
        Émile Nelligan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Groulx" title="Lionel Groulx">
        Lionel Groulx
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Roy" title="Gabrielle Roy">
        Gabrielle Roy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Aquin" title="Hubert Aquin">
        Hubert Aquin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Michel_Tremblay" title="Michel Tremblay">
        Michel Tremblay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marie_Laberge" title="Marie Laberge">
        Marie Laberge
       </a>
       , Fred Pellerin and
       <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Miron" title="Gaston Miron">
        Gaston Miron
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Literary_Regionalism" title="American Literary Regionalism">
        regional novel
       </a>
       from Quebec is called
       <i>
        Terroir
       </i>
       novel and is a literary tradition
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
        <a href="#cite_note-226">
         [226]
        </a>
       </sup>
       specific to the province. It includes such works as
       <i>
        The Old Canadians
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Maria_Chapdelaine" title="Maria Chapdelaine">
         Maria Chapdelaine
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A9raphin:_un_homme_et_son_p%C3%A9ch%C3%A9" title="Séraphin: un homme et son péché">
         Un homme et son péché
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Le Survenant
       </i>
       , etc. There are also many successful plays from this literary category, such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Les_Belles-s%C5%93urs" title="Les Belles-sœurs">
         Les Belles-sœurs
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Broue (Brew)
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the theatre troupes are the
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Duceppe" title="Jean Duceppe">
        Compagnie Jean-Duceppe
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        Théâtre La Rubrique
       </i>
       at the Pierrette-Gaudreault venue of the Institut of arts in Saguenay, the Théâtre Le Grenier, etc. In addition to the network of cultural centres in Quebec,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
        <a href="#cite_note-227">
         [227]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the venues include the
       <a href="/wiki/Monument-National" title="Monument-National">
        Monument-National
       </a>
       and the
       <i>
        Rideau Vert
       </i>
       (green curtain) Theatre in
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        Trident
       </i>
       Theatre in
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
        Quebec City
       </a>
       , etc. The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_School_of_Canada" title="National Theatre School of Canada">
        National Theatre School of Canada
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Conservatoire_de_musique_et_d%27art_dramatique_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Conservatoire de musique et d'art dramatique du Québec">
        Conservatoire de musique et d'art dramatique du Québec
       </a>
       form the future players.
      </p>
      <p>
       Popular French-language contemporary writers include
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Caron" title="Louis Caron">
        Louis Caron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Jacob" title="Suzanne Jacob">
        Suzanne Jacob
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yves_Beauchemin" title="Yves Beauchemin">
        Yves Beauchemin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Archambault" title="Gilles Archambault">
        Gilles Archambault
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Mavis_Gallant" title="Mavis Gallant">
        Mavis Gallant
       </a>
       , born in Quebec, lived in Paris from the 1950s onward. Well-known English-language writers from Quebec include
       <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cohen" title="Leonard Cohen">
        Leonard Cohen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mordecai_Richler" title="Mordecai Richler">
        Mordecai Richler
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Bissoondath" title="Neil Bissoondath">
        Neil Bissoondath
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:32px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lachassegalerie.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="640" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lachassegalerie.jpg/120px-Lachassegalerie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lachassegalerie.jpg/180px-Lachassegalerie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lachassegalerie.jpg/240px-Lachassegalerie.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Henri_Julien" title="Henri Julien">
            Henri Julien
           </a>
           ,
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Chasse-galerie" title="Chasse-galerie">
             La Chasse-galerie
            </a>
           </i>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="321" data-file-width="217" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg/81px-Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg/122px-Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg/162px-Emile_Nelligan_1.jpg 2x" width="81"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Nelligan" title="Émile Nelligan">
            Émile Nelligan
           </a>
           , Quebec poet, famous for his poem
           <i>
            Winter evening
           </i>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">
        Fine arts
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1999" data-file-width="1506" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/160px-Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/240px-Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/320px-Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Daudelin-Cavali%C3%A8re-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Charles_Daudelin" title="Charles Daudelin">
          Charles Daudelin
         </a>
         ,
         <i>
          La Cavalière
         </i>
         , 1963, Sculpture installed in front of the pavilion Gérard Morisset of the Quebec National Museum of Fine Arts in
         <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
          Quebec City
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       First influenced since the days of New France by Catholicism, with works from
       <i>
        Frère Luc
       </i>
       (Brother Luke) and more recently from
       <a href="/wiki/Ozias_Leduc" title="Ozias Leduc">
        Ozias Leduc
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guido_Nincheri" title="Guido Nincheri">
        Guido Nincheri
       </a>
       , art of Quebec has developed around the specific characteristics of its landscapes and cultural, historical, social and political representations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
        <a href="#cite_note-228">
         [228]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Thus, the development of Quebec masterpieces in painting, printmaking and sculpture is marked by the contribution of artists such as
       <a href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_H%C3%A9bert" title="Louis-Philippe Hébert">
        Louis-Philippe Hébert
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Krieghoff" title="Cornelius Krieghoff">
        Cornelius Krieghoff
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Lalibert%C3%A9" title="Alfred Laliberté">
        Alfred Laliberté
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc-Aur%C3%A8le_Fortin" title="Marc-Aurèle Fortin">
        Marc-Aurèle Fortin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc-Aur%C3%A8le_de_Foy_Suzor-Cot%C3%A9" title="Marc-Aurèle de Foy Suzor-Coté">
        Marc-Aurèle de Foy Suzor-Coté
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Paul_Lemieux" title="Jean Paul Lemieux">
        Jean Paul Lemieux
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Gagnon" title="Clarence Gagnon">
        Clarence Gagnon
       </a>
       , Adrien Dufresne,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pellan" title="Alfred Pellan">
        Alfred Pellan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean-Philippe_Dallaire" title="Jean-Philippe Dallaire">
        Jean-Philippe Dallaire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Daudelin" title="Charles Daudelin">
        Charles Daudelin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Villeneuve" title="Arthur Villeneuve">
        Arthur Villeneuve
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Riopelle" title="Jean-Paul Riopelle">
        Jean-Paul Riopelle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paul-%C3%89mile_Borduas" title="Paul-Émile Borduas">
        Paul-Émile Borduas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelle_Ferron" title="Marcelle Ferron">
        Marcelle Ferron
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">
        Fine arts
       </a>
       of Quebec are displayed at the
       <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_national_des_beaux-arts_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Musée national des beaux-arts du Québec">
        Quebec National Museum of Fine Arts
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_d%27art_contemporain_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Musée d'art contemporain de Montréal">
        Montreal Museum of Contemporary Art
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Montreal Museum of Fine Arts">
        Montreal Museum of Fine Arts
       </a>
       , the Quebec
       <i>
        Salon des métiers d'art
       </i>
       and in many art galleries. While many works decorate the public areas of Quebec, others are displayed in foreign countries such as the sculpture
       <i>
        Embâcle
       </i>
       (Jam) by Charles Daudelin on
       <i>
        Québec Place
       </i>
       in Paris and the statue
       <i>
        Québec Libre!
       </i>
       (free Quebec!) by
       <a href="/wiki/Armand_Vaillancourt" title="Armand Vaillancourt">
        Armand Vaillancourt
       </a>
       in San Francisco. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_des_Beaux-Arts_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="École des Beaux-Arts de Montréal">
        Montreal School of Fine Arts
       </a>
       forms the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_artists" title="List of Canadian artists">
        painters, printmakers and sculptors of Quebec
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Various buildings reflect the architectural heritage that characterizes Quebec, such as religious buildings, city halls, houses of large estates, and other locations throughout the province.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Circus_and_street_art">
        Circus and street art
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dralion-Vienna.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1333" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dralion-Vienna.jpg/220px-Dralion-Vienna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dralion-Vienna.jpg/330px-Dralion-Vienna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dralion-Vienna.jpg/440px-Dralion-Vienna.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dralion-Vienna.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The show
         <i>
          Dralion
         </i>
         , Cirque du Soleil, introduced in 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Several circus troupes were created in recent decades, the most important being without any doubt the
       <a href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil" title="Cirque du Soleil">
        Cirque du Soleil
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
        <a href="#cite_note-229">
         [229]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Among these troops are contemporary, travelling and on-horseback circuses, such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Les_7_Doigts_de_la_Main&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Les 7 Doigts de la Main (page does not exist)">
        Les 7 Doigts de la Main
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cirque_%C3%89loize" title="Cirque Éloize">
        Cirque Éloize
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cavalia" title="Cavalia">
        Cavalia
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Kosmogonia
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Saka
       </i>
       and Cirque
       <i>
        Akya
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
        <a href="#cite_note-230">
         [230]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Presented outdoors under a tent or in venues similar to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casino_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Casino de Montréal">
        Montreal Casino
       </a>
       , the circuses attract large crowds both in Quebec and abroad. In the manner of touring companies of the
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Clown" title="Clown">
        clowns
       </a>
       , street performers,
       <a href="/wiki/Minstrel" title="Minstrel">
        minstrels
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Troubadour" title="Troubadour">
        troubadours
       </a>
       travel from city to city to play their comedies. Although they may appear randomly from time to time during the year, they are always visible in the cultural events such as the Winterlude in Gatineau, the
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Winter_Carnival" title="Quebec Winter Carnival">
        Quebec Winter Carnival
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Gatineau_Hot_Air_Balloon_Festival" title="Gatineau Hot Air Balloon Festival">
        Gatineau Hot Air Balloon Festival
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City_Summer_Festival" title="Quebec City Summer Festival">
        Quebec City Summer Festival
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Just_for_Laughs" title="Just for Laughs">
        Just for Laughs Festival
       </a>
       in Montreal and the Festival of New France in Quebec.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_nationale_de_cirque" title="École nationale de cirque">
        National Circus School
       </a>
       and the
       <i>
        École de cirque de Québec
       </i>
       were created to train future
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_circus" title="Contemporary circus">
        Contemporary circus
       </a>
       artists. For its part,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tohu,_la_Cit%C3%A9_des_Arts_du_Cirque&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tohu, la Cité des Arts du Cirque (page does not exist)">
         Tohu, la Cité des Arts du Cirque
        </a>
       </i>
       was founded in 2004 to disseminate the circus arts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
        <a href="#cite_note-231">
         [231]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heritage">
        Heritage
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9pertoire_du_patrimoine_culturel_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Répertoire du patrimoine culturel du Québec">
        Répertoire du patrimoine culturel du Québec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_et_Archives_nationales_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Bibliothèque et Archives nationales du Québec">
        Bibliothèque et Archives nationales du Québec
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Val-Jalbert_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Val-Jalbert_2.jpg/220px-Val-Jalbert_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Val-Jalbert_2.jpg/330px-Val-Jalbert_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Val-Jalbert_2.jpg/440px-Val-Jalbert_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Val-Jalbert_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The school and the convent of the Congregation of Our Lady of Good Council, the ghost town of Val-Jalbert,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean" title="Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean">
          Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Cultural Heritage Fund is a program of the Quebec government
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
        <a href="#cite_note-232">
         [232]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for the conservation and development of Quebec's heritage, together with various laws.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
        <a href="#cite_note-233">
         [233]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several organizations ensure that same mission, both in the social and cultural traditions in the countryside and heritage buildings, including the
       <i>
        Commission des biens culturels du Québec
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Quebec Heritage Fondation
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Conservation Centre of Quebec
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Centre for development of living heritage
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Quebec Council of living heri tage
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Quebec Association of heritage interpretation
       </i>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       Several sites, houses and historical works reflect the cultural heritage of Quebec, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Village_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois_d%27Antan" title="Village Québécois d'Antan">
        Village Québécois d'Antan
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Val-Jalbert,_Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Val-Jalbert, Québec (page does not exist)">
        historical village of Val-Jalbert
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Chambly" title="Fort Chambly">
        Fort Chambly
       </a>
       , the national home of the Patriots, the Chicoutimi pulp mill (Pulperie de Chicoutimi), the
       <a href="/wiki/Lachine_Canal" title="Lachine Canal">
        Lachine Canal
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Bridge_(Montreal)" title="Victoria Bridge (Montreal)">
        Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       . Strongly influenced by the presence of the Catholic Church, the development of the religious history of Quebec is provided by organizations like the Council of the religious heritage of Quebec. Since 2007, the government promotes, with the various players in the field, the conclusion of agreements on the use of property belonging to episcopal factories and corporations to establish "
       <i>
        partnerships in financing the restoration and renovation of religious buildings
       </i>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
        <a href="#cite_note-234">
         [234]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of December 2011, there are 190
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada_in_Quebec" title="List of National Historic Sites of Canada in Quebec">
        National Historic Sites of Canada
       </a>
       in Quebec.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
        <a href="#cite_note-235">
         [235]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These sites were designated as being of national historic significance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
        <a href="#cite_note-236">
         [236]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Various museums tell the cultural history of Quebec, like the
       <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_la_civilisation" title="Musée de la civilisation">
        Museum of Civilization
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Musée de l'Amérique française">
        Museum of French America
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/McCord_Museum" title="McCord Museum">
        McCord Museum
       </a>
       or the Montreal Museum of Archaeology and History in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pointe-%C3%A0-Calli%C3%A8re" title="Pointe-à-Callière">
        Pointe-à-Callière
       </a>
       , displaying artifacts, paintings and other remains from the past of Quebec. Many literary works reproduce the daily lives of the past, following the social and cultural traditions of Quebec television series reproducing the old days
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
        <a href="#cite_note-237">
         [237]
        </a>
       </sup>
       such as the trilogy of
       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gauvreau" title="Pierre Gauvreau">
        Pierre Gauvreau
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Le Temps d'une paix
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Cormoran
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Le Volcan tranquille
       </i>
       ),
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Famille_Plouffe" title="La Famille Plouffe">
         La Famille Plouffe
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Les_Belles_Histoires_des_pays_d%27en_haut" title="Les Belles Histoires des pays d'en haut">
         Les Belles Histoires des Pays-d'en-Haut
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Petite_Patrie" title="La Petite Patrie">
         La Petite Patrie
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Entre chien et loup
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Les_Filles_de_Caleb" title="Les Filles de Caleb">
         Les Filles de Caleb
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Blanche
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Au nom du père et du fils
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Marguerite Volant
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Nos Étés
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Musée Éden
       </i>
       , among others.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Quebec" title="Cuisine of Quebec">
        Cuisine of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1028" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg/220px-La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg/330px-La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg/440px-La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Banquise_Poutine.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A classic
         <a href="/wiki/Poutine" title="Poutine">
          poutine
         </a>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/La_Banquise" title="La Banquise">
          La Banquise
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
          Montreal
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG/220px-Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG/330px-Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG/440px-Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schwartz_smoked_meat_montreal.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Montreal-style smoked meat from
         <a href="/wiki/Schwartz%27s" title="Schwartz's">
          Schwartz's
         </a>
         in Montreal.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The historical context of 'traditional' Quebec cuisine is from the fur trade period and many dishes have a high fat or lard content. From the early 17th century, French settlers populating North America were interested in a new cuisine to confront the climate and the needs arising from the work of colonization. Mindful of the same nutritional needs as settlers from
       <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">
        Acadia
       </a>
       , it has many similarities with Acadian cuisine. Quebec's cuisine has a strong French and Irish influence, although many aspects of Canadian aboriginal cuisine have also had a significant impact on Quebec cuisine. Quebec is most famous for its
       <a href="/wiki/Tourti%C3%A8re" title="Tourtière">
        Tourtière
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C3%A2t%C3%A9_Chinois" title="Pâté Chinois">
        Pâté Chinois
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Poutine" title="Poutine">
        Poutine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/St._Catherine%27s_taffy" title="St. Catherine's taffy">
        St. Catherine's taffy
       </a>
       among others. The temps des sucres (sugar season) is one of the oldest of Quebec culinary traditions. During springtime, many Quebecers go to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_house" title="Sugar house">
        cabane à sucre
       </a>
       (sugar house) for a traditional meal. The Jewish community of
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       has contributed
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal-style_bagel" title="Montreal-style bagel">
        Montreal-style bagels
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Smoked_meat" title="Smoked meat">
        smoked meat
       </a>
       which is similar to
       <a href="/wiki/Pastrami" title="Pastrami">
        pastrami
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec has produced beer since the beginning of colonization especially with the emergence of
       <a href="/wiki/Spruce_beer" title="Spruce beer">
        spruce beer
       </a>
       . In 1668,
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Talon" title="Jean Talon">
        Jean Talon
       </a>
       founded a brewery in Quebec City, but it closed a decade later. Although many people tried to produce a beer between the 17th and 18th centuries, it is only since the 1980s that the industries had produced on a larger scale. Today there are nearly a hundred breweries and companies, including
       <a href="/wiki/Unibroue" title="Unibroue">
        Unibroue
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molson_Coors" title="Molson Coors">
        Molson Coors
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labatt" title="Labatt">
        Labatt
       </a>
       and many others. Quebec also produces wine,
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_wine" title="Ice wine">
        ice wine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_cider" title="Ice cider">
        ice cider
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Quebec has produced cheese for centuries. The first cheese-making school in North America was established in Saint-Denis-de-Kamouraska in 1893. It was at this moment that the monks of La Trappe of Oka began to produce the famous
       <a href="/wiki/Oka_cheese" title="Oka cheese">
        Oka cheese
       </a>
       . Today there are over 300 different cheeses in Quebec.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg/220px-Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg/330px-Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg/440px-Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boston_vs._CH_au_Centre_Bell_007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Canadiens" title="Montreal Canadiens">
          Montreal Canadiens
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Bell_Centre" title="Bell Centre">
          Bell Centre
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Sports in Quebec constitutes an essential dimension of Quebec culture. The practice of sports and outdoor activities in Quebec was influenced largely by its geography and climate.
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">
        Ice hockey
       </a>
       remains the national sport. This sport, which was played for the first time on March 3, 1875, at the Victoria Skating Rink in Montreal and promoted over the years by numerous achievements of the centenary of the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Canadiens" title="Montreal Canadiens">
        Montreal Canadiens
       </a>
       , still raises passions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
        <a href="#cite_note-238">
         [238]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other major sports include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Football" title="Canadian Football">
        Canadian Football
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">
        Montreal Alouettes
       </a>
       , soccer with the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Impact" title="Montreal Impact">
        Montreal Impact
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="Canadian Grand Prix">
        Grand Prix du Canada
       </a>
       Formula 1 racing with drivers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Villeneuve" title="Gilles Villeneuve">
        Gilles Villeneuve
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Villeneuve" title="Jacques Villeneuve">
        Jacques Villeneuve
       </a>
       , and professional baseball with the former
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">
        Montreal Expos
       </a>
       . During its history, Quebec has hosted several major sporting events; including the
       <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">
        1976 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       , the Fencing World Championships in 1967, track cycling in 1974, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transat_Qu%C3%A9bec-Saint-Malo" title="Transat Québec-Saint-Malo">
        Transat Québec-Saint-Malo
       </a>
       race created for the first time in 1984.
      </p>
      <p>
       Québec athletes have performed well at the
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">
        Winter Olympics
       </a>
       over recent years. They won 12 of
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2018_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2018 Winter Olympics">
        Canada's 29 medals
       </a>
       at the most recent
       <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">
        Winter Olympics in Pyeongchang (2018)
       </a>
       ; they won 12 of the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2014_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2014 Winter Olympics">
        27 Canadian medals
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">
        Sochi (2014)
       </a>
       ; and 9 of the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2010 Winter Olympics">
        26 Canadian medals
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">
        Vancouver (2010)
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
        <a href="#cite_note-239">
         [239]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">
        National symbols
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Symbols_of_Quebec" title="Symbols of Quebec">
        Symbols of Quebec
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fleur_de_lys_du_qu%C3%A9bec.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="299" data-file-width="219" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Fleur_de_lys_du_qu%C3%A9bec.png/170px-Fleur_de_lys_du_qu%C3%A9bec.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Fleur_de_lys_du_qu%C3%A9bec.png 1.5x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fleur_de_lys_du_qu%C3%A9bec.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Fleur-de-lys
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1939, the
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Quebec" title="Government of Quebec">
        government of Quebec
       </a>
       unilaterally ratified its
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Quebec" title="Coat of arms of Quebec">
        coat of arms
       </a>
       to reflect
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Quebec" title="History of Quebec">
        Quebec's political history
       </a>
       : French rule (gold lily on blue background), British rule (lion on red background) and Canadian rule (maple leaves) and with Quebec's motto below "Je me souviens".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
        <a href="#cite_note-240">
         [240]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Je_me_souviens" title="Je me souviens">
        Je me souviens
       </a>
       ("I remember") was first carved under the coat of arms of Quebec's
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Building_(Quebec)" title="Parliament Building (Quebec)">
        Parliament Building
       </a>
       façade in 1883. It is an official part of the coat of arms and has been the official licence plate motto since 1978, replacing "
       <i>
        La belle province
       </i>
       " (the beautiful province). The expression
       <i>
        La belle province
       </i>
       is still used mostly in tourism as a nickname for the province.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag-of-Quebec.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag-of-Quebec.jpg/170px-Flag-of-Quebec.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag-of-Quebec.jpg/255px-Flag-of-Quebec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag-of-Quebec.jpg/340px-Flag-of-Quebec.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag-of-Quebec.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Quebec" title="Flag of Quebec">
           Fleurdelisé
          </a>
         </b>
         flying at
         <a href="/wiki/Place_d%27Armes" title="Place d'Armes">
          Place d'Armes
         </a>
         in Montreal.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The fleur-de-lis, the ancient symbol of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_monarchy" title="French monarchy">
        French monarchy
       </a>
       , first arrived on the shores of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9sie" title="Gaspésie">
        Gaspésie
       </a>
       in 1534 with
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">
        Jacques Cartier
       </a>
       on his first voyage. When
       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">
        Samuel de Champlain
       </a>
       founded
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec_City" title="Québec City">
        Québec City
       </a>
       in 1608, his ship hoisted the merchant flag of a white cross on a blue background. By 1758 at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carillon" title="Battle of Carillon">
        Battle of Carillon
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Carillon" title="Flag of Carillon">
        Flag of Carillon
       </a>
       would become the basis of Quebec's desire to have its own flag. By 1903, the parent of today's flag had taken shape, known as the "
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fleurdelis%C3%A9" title="Fleurdelisé">
         Fleurdelisé
        </a>
       </i>
       ". The flag in its present form with its 4 white "
       <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">
        fleur-de-lis
       </a>
       " lilies on a blue background with a white cross replaced the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">
        Union Jack
       </a>
       on Quebec's
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Building_(Quebec)" title="Parliament Building (Quebec)">
        Parliament Building
       </a>
       on January 21, 1948.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_official_symbols">
        Other official symbols
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The floral emblem of Quebec is the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Iris_versicolor" title="Iris versicolor">
          Iris versicolor
         </a>
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qsymbols_7-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Qsymbols-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Since 1987 the avian emblem of Quebec has been the
        <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">
         snowy owl
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qsymbols_7-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-Qsymbols-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        An official tree, the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_birch" title="Yellow birch">
         yellow birch
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         bouleau jaune
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         merisier
        </i>
        ), symbolizes the importance Quebecers give to the forests. The tree is known for the variety of its uses and commercial value, as well as its autumn colours.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qsymbols_7-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-Qsymbols-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In 1998 the
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Insectarium" title="Montreal Insectarium">
        Montreal Insectarium
       </a>
       sponsored a poll to choose an official insect. The
       <a href="/wiki/Limenitis_arthemis" title="Limenitis arthemis">
        white admiral
       </a>
       butterfly (
       <i>
        Limenitis arthemis
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
        <a href="#cite_note-241">
         [241]
        </a>
       </sup>
       won with 32% of the 230 660 votes against the spotted
       <a href="/wiki/Coccinellidae" title="Coccinellidae">
        lady beetle
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Coleomegilla maculata lengi
       </i>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Ebony_jewelwing" title="Ebony jewelwing">
        ebony jewelwing
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Damselfly" title="Damselfly">
        damselfly
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Calopteryx maculata
       </i>
       ), a species of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bumble_bee" title="Bumble bee">
        bumble bee
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Bombus impatiens
       </i>
       ) and the six-spotted
       <a href="/wiki/Tiger_beetle" title="Tiger beetle">
        tiger beetle
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Cicindela sexguttata sexguttata
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="F.C3.AAte_nationale_.28National_Holiday.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fête_nationale_(National_Holiday)">
        Fête nationale (National Holiday)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Holiday_(Quebec)" title="National Holiday (Quebec)">
        National Holiday (Quebec)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1977, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_Parliament" title="Quebec Parliament">
        Quebec Parliament
       </a>
       declared June 24 to be Quebec's National Holiday. Historically June 24 was a holiday honouring French Canada's patron saint,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John_the_Baptist" title="St. John the Baptist">
        St. John the Baptist
       </a>
       , which is why it is commonly known as
       <i>
        La Saint-Jean-Baptiste
       </i>
       (often shortened to
       <i>
        La St-Jean
       </i>
       ). On this day, the song "
       <a href="/wiki/Gens_du_pays" title="Gens du pays">
        Gens du pays
       </a>
       " by
       <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Vigneault" title="Gilles Vigneault">
        Gilles Vigneault
       </a>
       is often heard and commonly regarded as Quebec's unofficial anthem. The festivities occur on June 23 and 24 and are celebrated all over Quebec. In cities like
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
        Québec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montréal
       </a>
       , great shows are organized in the main public places (such as the Abraham plains,
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
        Québec
       </a>
       , or Maisonneuve Park,
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montréal
       </a>
       ) where several of the most popular Quebec artists relay each others
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2012)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       until late at night.
      </p>

          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-oedpron_8-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation" id="CITEREFReference-OED-Quebec">
           <a class="external text" href="http://oed.com/search?searchType=dictionary&amp;q=Quebec" rel="nofollow">
            "Quebec"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">
             Oxford English Dictionary
            </a>
           </i>
           (3rd ed.).
           <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">

          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Quebec&amp;rft.btitle=Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.edition=3rd&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2005-09&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Foed.com%2Fsearch%3FsearchType%3Ddictionary%26q%3DQuebec&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AQuebec">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="font-size:0.95em; font-size:90%; color:#555">
           (Subscription or
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.oxforddnb.com/help/subscribe#public" rel="nofollow">
            UK public library membership
           </a>
           required.)
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-EFname-9">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-EFname_9-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          According to the
          <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">
           Canadian government
          </a>
          ,
          <b>
           Québec
          </b>
          (with the
          <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
           acute accent
          </a>
          ) is the official name in
          <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">
           French
          </a>
          and
          <b>
           Quebec
          </b>
          (without the accent) is the province's official name in
          <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">
           English
          </a>
          ; the name is
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.nrcan.gc.ca/earth-sciences/geography/place-names/useful-material-translators/9232" rel="nofollow">
           one of 81 locales of pan-Canadian significance with official forms in both languages
          </a>
          . In this system, the official name of the
          <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">
           capital is Québec
          </a>
          in both official languages. The Government of Quebec renders both names as
          <i>
           Québec
          </i>
          in both languages.
         </span>
        </li>

         <span class="reference-text">
          "his Most Christian Majesty cedes and guaranties to his said Britannick Majesty, in full right, Canada, with all its dependencies, as well as the island of Cape Breton, and all the other islands and coasts in the gulph and river of St. Lawrence, and in general, every thing that depends on the said countries, lands, islands, and coasts, with the sovereignty, property, possession, and all rights acquired by treaty, or otherwise, which the Most Christian King and the Crown of France have had till now over the said countries, lands, islands, places, coasts, and their inhabitants" –
          <i>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="s:Treaty of Paris (1763)">
            Treaty of Paris
           </a>
